##

2018-01-05 13:07:16
Baisali Mukherjee
35581445
4.5
There is nothing new I can add for this age-old eatery - this is an iconic restaurant in food map of Kolkata, conveniently located at Mullickbazar crossing on the Park street side. For the last 75 years it has established itself as the most famous Biriyani joint in Calcutta. We visited this one during or winter vacation to Calcutta. Recently after renovation it has become more comfortable and modern looking. On weekends the size of the queue outside it is quite sizable. The most famous menu options are Chicken Biriyani, Mutton Rezala, Chicken chap, Firni and Haleem. We ordered a Chicken biriyani, a Special Chicken Biriyani ( extra portion, one more chicken piece and egg as special addition), Rezala, Tandoori Roti and Carrot Halwa. Everything was excellently tasty except the halwa. The service was excellent and fast, seating was little congested but overall ambience was good. The price has increased over time but still is not overtly expensive. One special mention should be made for its fluffy rotis which is excellently soft. BTW, there is a parking place just opposite to the restaurant which is rare in such a busy junction. I would give a 4.5 rating.

##

2017-12-29 11:56:20
Saurodeep Basak
1507076
3.0
Well nothing's much to say for this age-old eatery. The name's synonymous just like Sourav Ganguly is to Kolkata! So without exploring into details of it's ambiance and service (never expected something great), let's pounce upon the dishes which we tasted. 


We were a bunch of misfits. So we started off with a cup of tea which is very much weird thing to do in a place like this! Nevertheless the tea was good. While we were chatting over a cuppa, our food came rather disturbingly! You must be thinking why I said so! Go on read the rest, you'll know why! 


We, just "bheto-bangalis", ordered Mutton Biryani and Chicken chaap straightaway. While some of us, the non rice lovers opted for something different. They took Tandoori rotis compliled with Chicken Bharta, Mutton Qorma and even Palak Paneer! Yeah you heard that right! What an audacity!! 


1. Mutton Biryani was usual typical of Shiraz. Greasy, aromatic and difficult to rub off your hands of that intoxicating smell once you finish it. 

2. Chicken chaap - God knows why I order this everytime! Knowing fully it's quite an average dish, I still go for it. A Bengali's issue maybe! 

3. Chicken Bharta and Mutton Qorma seemed to bond well with Tandoori rotis, as our misfit lots were licking their fingers by now! However, they were heard cursing the Mutton rezala (which they ordered later). 

4. After a hearty plate of biryani, my typical bongo tummy was full but mind? Not so much! So there you go!! Another order of Tandoori Roti and Kashmiri Chicken. Kashmiri Chicken was not at all Kashmiri left alone the white texture! Though it tasted good. 

5. Now coming to the abomination part. Palak Paneer! Yeah you guessed right! Total disaster as recalled by our vegetarian freak in our midst. 


Now, moving on to the dessert section, we took (like everytime) firnis and a Shahi tukra for a chaand-ka-tukra of our pack! Though she has quite a sweet tooth, still it pained us to see go through the "shahi treatment" alone! Firni on the other hand, was fine as usual. 

And thus concluding our hunger pangs! If you visit Park Street and happen to crave for a bite on mangsho, you can definitely give this place a try! If not for that, then do it for the sake of 'nostalgia', silly!

2017-11-29 00:21:42
Pranjal Dey
33598599
1.5
To a person who's visiting Shiraz for the first time, beware of their staff. They have no idea how to describe an item. Almost all items are in some way similar to each other according to these great people wearing suits. I would rather prefer asking the guys in yellow dresses for descriptions of any item. The Biryani festival going on currently(till 30th Nov, 2017) had been on my mind since i came across it in the newspaper a few days ago. Finally made up some time to go try out these new additions. I have always sworn by their mutton biryani and no doubt the regular items on their menu are good.
The biryani festival however according to me has turned out to be a big disaster for them. This can be attributable to their floor staff and their extremely unprofessional like conduct. They are least bothered about explaining what an item might actually taste like. Personally i doubt whether they have ever tasted any item appearing in their menu card. Otherwise how the hell will you explain the nitty-gritties of any dish?
As a person who has visited every south indian state and also has had every kind of biryani on offer down south i can tell you that a Hyderabadi Biryani is red in colour and super spicy. This makes it distinguishable from the other types of biryani. Shiraz however turned out a yellow polao like dish resembling an Awadhi Biryani look and that is their take on Hyderabadi Biryani which was also like a bit sweet instead of the usual hot n spicy. Fyi Hyderabadi cuisine is known for its extensive use of spices and chilly.
The other 2 dishes ordered were indistinguishable from each other. Saadi Biryani and Moti biryani. Super bland.
Only the Ambur Biryani turned out to be spicy and tasty.
The floor managers need to learn a thing or two about manners. When a customer asks the staff for suggestions after pointing out exactly what kind of dish he/she is looking for, it is the duty of the floor staff to understand the wants and adequately explain which item(s) fulfil the customer's criteria. When you're extremely unprofessional and do not give a damn as to what the customer wants and also have no clue as to what's actually on the menu then how do have the audacity to ask for tips? 
This after we had brought it to their attention that their suggestions were absolutely useless and they had absolutely no idea about what they were trying to sell.

##

2017-11-12 20:49:03
Sayantan Ghosh
34553906
4.0
There are some chains and outlets which are synonymous with the thriving biriyani culture of Kolkata. Royal, Arsalan, Aminia, Rahmania, and Shiraz form the golden pentagon of Kolkata in this category.

Shiraz is one of the oldest, most recognized, and most popular brand names when it comes to biriyani in Kolkata. It was launched in 1941 as the Taj Restaurant. About 15 years later, it renamed itself as The Golden Restaurant. Further down the road, it finally came to call itself Shiraz - The Golden Restaurant, but to most biriyani enthusiasts (and, in general, the populace) of Kolkata, it is simply known as Shiraz.

Mutton Biriyani: Shiraz serves your to typical Kolkata biriyani, which is sort of a variant of the Lucknowi Dum Biriyani popularized in Kolkata by the exiled Nawab of Lucknow Wajid Ali Shah and his royal chefs. It is prepared in the dum pukht method, i. e., in containers sealed with wheat flour dough slow cooked over a low fire. Fine, long-grained, aromatic basmati rice lightly flavoured with Indian spices like cloves, cardamom and saffron is cooked together with large, succulent pieces of mutton, so that the flavours of the rice, spices and meat mix with each other to give you an amazingly delicious taste. The biriyani in Shiraz is much more subtle in its flavour and aroma than most other biriyani outlets. It is also has lower greasiness, but it makes their biriyani slightly hard and dry, and perhaps just a bit difficult to swallow without a gravy on the side. A large piece of potato and a boiled egg is served with your biriyani in signature Kolkata biriyani style.

Now, truth be told, you'll probably find a few places in Kolkata which serve better biriyani than Shiraz. And you'll surely find a lot of places which serve better kababs. But when it comes to sides, Shiraz is at the top of their game.

Here are a few sides from Shiraz that I've tried:

1. Mutton Pasinda: Thin succulent strips of mutton in a rich, spicy almond paste gravy, this is my favourite side dish at Shiraz. The strips are marinated with curd and soak up the flavours of spices and ghee (Indian clarified butter) used in the gravy. The almond paste gravy is spiced with rich, flavourful spices like cardamom, cloves, cumin, coriander, cinnamon, nutmeg, pepper, green chillies and garlic. The mutton and gravy are cooked in ghee, and you can literally see the red, oily ghee grease floating at the bottom of the container. The dish has an amazing, tangy taste, and the thin spicy, mutton strips simply melt in your mouth.

2. Mutton liver fry: This is a simple but delicious dish. It is basically lightly fried pieces of mutton liver cooked in a rich, spicy onion gravy. Tastes especially great with their roomali roti.

3. Mutton Tikia: This is an extremely cheap, but extremely tasty dish. This is basically a deep fried spicy minced mutton patty. The minced mutton is mixed with gram flour, eggs and onion-garlic-ginger puree, and spiced up with pepper, red pepper, chilli flakes, green chillies, bay leaves, cinnamon, cloves, and cardamom. Then this is mixed into a dough, made into a thick patty, and deep fried in hydrogenated vegetable oil. Simply delicious!

2017-11-04 18:05:32
Kaushik Chakraborty
40405573
3.5
It is a quite familiar name recently shrouded by multifarious greenhorns. But it still holds a striking rating. I felt intrigued and paid a visit. It was during the Durga Puja. But I had a great trouble to drop by there.The address is Park street but its far from the park street metro. At Mallick Bazar crossing. So,taking a cab would be a good option.

We ordered Chicken reshmi kabab, a butter naan, Chicken tikka Masala and a Chicken Biriyani.
Gorging on the food my 'intrigue' get cleared. Yes,the dishes were delectable. Especially the kabab and Chicken biriyani. Biriyani was light with a fascinating aroma. Blended with perfect spices. The pieces of kebabs were soft. Tasty.

Conclusion: I think this joint maintains their consistency and thus enjoying a 4 point rating. You can try kebabs and biriyani here. You won't regret. Rs.750 for Two persons will be enough.

This is the Led Zeplin of eateries serving Mughal cuisine in Kolkata. I have had the Chicken and Mutton Biryani, Naan& Rotis, Kebabs, Mutton Stew, Mutton Chaap, Chicken Rezala , Raita and Firni.

Ambience- Pleasant.
Overall- A must visit. Its the city's biryani at its best

*Starter : Chicken tengdi kebab
*Main course : Mutton Kasha
Kadai Chicken
*Chicken Biriyani
*Dessert : Firni

¬†

It is in this context that I wish to share an interesting experience....a neighbour arranged for Shiraz‚Äôs biryani at his wedding banquet. It was a special order, because the rest of the food items were commissioned to another caterer. The chef came to the wedding venue with his own utensils & ingredients, and cooked the biryani there. Both my father and I found this biryani to be excellent....far superior to the takeaway stuff that I used to bring home till then. This made us ponder whether the chefs at Shiraz cook different grades of biryani for different occasions. If that is the case, they are doing a disservice to ordinary customers who are meted out food of an average quality.

2017-05-30 00:05:26
Sayak Chakraborty
33181481
4.0
I have been here a few times. The decor and ambience is very sophisticated and the entire crew is very friendly and hospitable. Everything about them makes you feel at ease and peace especially if you make your way around the afternoon or so. But dinner time or the times post-sunset during Ramzan, it literally explodes into activitu and a busy hubbub.
The food is not very spicy at Shiraz. The biryani, especially the mutton one, is probably one of the best that can be had in this city. Theur mutton side dishes are really flavourful and the meat is of the finest quality and always happens to be tender and succulent. Their lamb/mutton brain curry is something of a stand out, for me. It's has a sweet gravy with the brain chunks being very fatty and gives a funny feeling in the mouth. One is recommended to try it, but at their own risk only.
I don't like their plain rotis much but the tandoori roti or naan and parathas are really commendable.
Shiraz has been golden for long and given their form, I feel they'll continue to be so for the times to come.

##

2017-02-05 20:22:12
Sumana Bera
35329654
5.0
If you want a plateful of biriyani with its own personality, go to Shiraz. Seriously. I can recognize their biriyani in a blind tasting. They have a distinct aroma and richness to their food, which is probably because of the ghee they use. This is not a biriyani for someone who abhors oil and richness. This is for someone who wants decadent mutton biriyani. If you want biriyani cooked with mathematical precision and perfection, Arsalan is the place to go. Shiraz's biriyani is the one cooked like a traditionalist, it's meant to be rich and oily. In fact, I usually need a gravy dish like chicken chaanp to go with my biriyani, but not here.
Their kebabs are also cooked beautifully with heavy aromatic flavours. Recently they offer chicken kathi kebabs, which pairs perfectly with their flaky parathas. Prices are on the higher end, but it's worth every cent.

The food was awesomely tasty and really justified the price they charge for the food items. However, I personally liked the Brain Fry above all else. It was simply too delicious. The biryani was good as it was not very oily but a little less spicy than expected.

A visit is recommended.

4.5
If you‚Äôre coming from sealdah, take the road towards AJC Bose road and you‚Äôll find Mullikbazar crossing, from there, turn left and the second/third shop is Siraz. From park circus crossing, take the park street and the first signal after park circus is mullikbazar crossing. Siraz is at your right-hand-side. It operates from morning 530 AM- 10 PM in the evening on all days

Just get in, choose any of the sofa and order for the Siraz special biryani (eyes closed). This comes with 2 pcs of meat (chicken/ mutton), rice, 1 potato (the integral part of kolkata biryani) and recently they‚Äôve started giving 1 boiled egg (god knows why). This is probably the second most subtle biryani in Kolkata, extremely lightly spiced, yellow and white rice mixed, its a treat for the eye as well for the smell‚Ä¶. forget about the tastebud. You‚Äôll just fall in love with it by just the smell. I‚Äôve been there probably hundred times and still am little hyper about this place. The meat size (for chicken especially) is a little smaller compared to a few other joints, but taste and aroma makes up for it.¬†

For heaven‚Äôs sake, please do not order champ with it, the champ, though being a great food at his own, just kills the mildness. This biryani goes extremely well with the mixed raita. The Siraz Raita is spicy, yet having the correct blend of sweetness (depicting bengali woman ??? ). They make a pretty good paratha and mutton kalia too, but once you‚Äôve found the champ, who cares for the second place holder ?

Firni(6/10): Taste-wise good but, it had big chunks of rice like you find in 'Paayesh' which isn't an attribute of firni.

My last visit to this restaurant in 2015 was still better than this one, with good amount of biryani, delicious firni and reshmi butter masala. The tomato in the salad back then was stale.

‚èπThe Firni here, too, is absolutely delicious and adds to a nice finishing to the meal.

Shiraz needs no introduction when it comes to Biryani and Indian food. 

This is the oldest outlet located near Mullick bazar which has been renovated in recent years.

Though I have been here on multiple occasions, I am writing today about a recent visit.

Me along with a very close friend came down at around 11:30 at night on a Sunday looking for some heavy dinner while we were at Neotia hospital nearby. On asking for a table at first they were a little confused, as it was pretty late but quickly gave us a table and took our order. As it was late the only option available was Biryani and along with that the Mutton Kassa was our side dish which was flown out of kitchen just at the blink of an eye. 

Huge quantity on the plate with soft mutton pieces along and a big alo made it a lip smacking affair. Wow!!! Even if I am not a Biryani lover just loved it.  The mutton kassa was made very light and did absolute justice as a side dish. Loved it totally and thus once again they proved why they have been carrying forward the legacy with them. ##

2016-11-09 23:45:45
Abhrodip Chaudhury
2272296
4.0
Imagine yourself to be a fan of mughal dishes, such as me (think huge). Now think of all of the most delicious flavours you want to ever taste in your life. Take those all together, ugh! you have the murgh musallam of this place! Ok enough with the PPAP cover. Shiraz is one of the best biriyani outlets in Kolkata and if you've tasted it, you don't need zomato to tell you it's legendary. This was my 2nd visit to this place, and i don't really know why i didn't write the review the 1st time (don't look at me like that :|). Shiraz does try to maintain some high standards with respect to not only their cooking but also service and ambience, however one thing that hurts that is a small part of the crowd that visits this place (i'm only talking about those who ogle others' food and murmur the names of the dishes which you have ordered while sitting at neighbouring tables, making you feel incredibly awkward...the rest of you are absolute darlings). The interior deco and table arrangement is all pretty nice. The service is really good with polite and helpful waiters and is pretty prompt. Now coming to the food. Biriyani over here is brilliant. I absolutely love it and I really feel it's one of the best you can find in Kolkata. But today was about something way more special - Murgh Musallam, that one dish that combines all layers and folds and niches of epicness in itself, and amplifies it to a mindblowing creation of human kind. Now the dish has to be ordered beforehand (i ordered about a day ahead, but i believe that's not the minimum limit), with the procedure followed here being pretty easy and straightforward: go, order, pay an amount as advance, and try to keep a leash on your salivary glands while you wait. I promise you won't be disappointed. The chicken was well cooked, nice and juicy and succulent, and the taste! It's all of those flavours you may crave for in mughal salans, stimulating taste buds slowly and in the most heavenly torture possible. Also, the egg inside is cooked separately and has a very low probability of being that chicken's own egg. Yes i had someone who was confused. All jokes apart, they said it was their specialty. They delivered. And they made the experience really special for us while they were at it.

2016-10-31 10:21:43
Debasree Chatterjee
33868748
4.0
Its an old inveterate famous restaurant known for the rich taste of its dishes. If you have a fetish for Mughlai cuisine, one must definitely try out this place to cherish some sterling and exceptional food.

Its located in Mullickbazaar crossing and is always on high demand for its reputation over the years. Its a two storey AC restaurant not much to do with the decor. But its really difficult to get a place and the most coveted dishes are always sold out quickly.

Driven by the speciality of this restaurant we decided on our order list. We took tandoori chicken, chicken reshmi kabab, butter naan, tandoori roti, mutton rezala, chicken rezala and chicken biriyani acompanied with green salad.

Tandoori chicken was simply mouth watering. It had the right marination and blend of spices which made the dish palatable. The rezalas were empyrean and blissful. It was so well cooked that you cant resist yourself from going on relishing it. Both the chicken and mutton was tender and succulent but the broth was to die for.
After rejoicing the dish, we took the biriyani. It was quite nice but the rezalla stole the show. The butter naan was very supple and lisome and could be easily ripped off. To be very honest, each of the items was worth praising.
I feel its one of the best place to cherish some delicious food and you should go with a good apetite to enjoy its flavourous dishes. Would surely visit this place again whenever I an there in Kolkata.

2016-07-16 12:52:22
Sumit Sehgal (foodiesumit)
2203362
2.0
This was my first time in Kolkata, and everyone I know who had visited Kolkata before told me to try Shiraz coz they are supposedly the best in serving food in Park Street, Kolkata and so we did.

Don't expect ambiance of any sort, just tables and chair and food is what you'll get.

We ordered three things here. A Mutton Biryani, a Chicken Biryani and Tandoori Fish.

‚Ä¢ Mutton & Chicken Biryani
I won't review them separately as there wasn't much difference between the two. When you hear the word biryani, all the spices and condiments come to your mind but nothing as such was here in Shiraz‚Äôs biryani. The spices used were very mild and the biryani looked more like plain colored rice. I know many of you would disagree with me, but I didn't find anything worth trying in it. And who puts a full boiled potato in the biryani? Maybe Shiraz thought of replacing the chicken/mutton piece with the potato as there was only one piece of chicken/mutton in the whole biryani. I mean what the hell? They didn't even serve raita or any curry with it and we ended up eating the biryani dry. Not a good experience indeed.

‚Ä¢ Tandoori Fish
The fish experience whereas not as bad as the biryani experience. The fish served with onions and mint chutney was soft and juicy, full of spices and we loved eating it.


Damage Done: 680 bucks.


Overall Rating: 2/5


Even if you don't visit, you're not missing anything.

2016-06-09 21:35:03
Debanjan Acharya
2379192
4.0
I was planning for a lunch in some moghlai restaurant with my girl friend and ultimately we finalized this place. Its a prominent and pronounced place located at the crossing of mallickbazar. Seating space is sufficient which includes arrangement in ground floor and 1st floor so unless there's a lot of crowd one need not to wait outside. Ac is centralised and temperature well controlled. Waiters are polite, Service is prompt and almost no waiting thats the best part.
Coming to the main part 'The Food': we ordered a plate of chicken malai til kebab one chicken biriyani and one mutton biriyani. Kebab was soft and flavours coming out well. The biriyani was perfect kolkata biriyani. It was light, flavours were perfect, the aloo and mutton was was well cooked and thus very soft. U get 200ml coke free with a plate of biriyani, this is an offer going on. So it was a perfect lunch. Prices are reasonable compared to the quality and quantity of food. Looking forward to visit this place really soon to try their mutton halim with roomali roti.

2016-06-06 17:51:01
Soham Ghosh
1833872
3.5
Let the record show that this particular Shiraz is the best in Kolkata. It absolutely demolishes any competition from its sister shops elsewhere. In terms of Biryani shops in Kolkata, Shiraz is definitely up there with the best, although it remains to be seen how well they fare over a longer period with stiff competition.

Shiraz's food is without question, brilliant. There can be no argument regarding the pure quality of foodstuff, or the portions they provide. For a premium Biryani joint, they manage to dish out a very large quantity of Biryani at the premium price. They're also pretty well received on the Chaap front -- I personally prefer their mutton over their chicken. The Chicken chaap is pretty standard, and does nothing to thrill. The mutton chaap however packs a larger punch and is basically more edible. But if you're a Chicken fanatic, you're probably going to order Chicken chaap anyway. Side note, they make a damn good Tikkia as well.

I've never sat and eaten at Shiraz, but I've been to the place. Therefore, I cannot quite disclose service stats.

Ambience/Interiors: 3.5/5
Service: n/a
Food: 4/5
Value for Money: 3/5

Thanks for reading and pardon me for any grammatical errors I may have made.

Went to Shiraz yesterday with family for dinner (my second visit after almost 9 years). Thank God we reached almost at thenick of time because in 10 minutes or so, the seats started filling up fast. We ordered for Shiraz Special Chicken Kebab (‚Çπ 275) and Mutton Boti Kebab (‚Çπ250) and both were served with green chutney, pickle and slices of onion. The Shiraz Special was supposed to be a chicken kebab with cheese (as per the person who took our order) did neither looked nor tasted so (the Arsalan Special is 100 times better than this) and the Mutton Boti needed some more cooking. Next for the main course, we ordered Chicken Biriyani (‚Çπ175), Mutton Biriyani (‚Çπ180), Chicken Rezala(‚Çπ160) and Mutton Pasinda(‚Çπ220). The biriyani quantity was huge with good chunks of meat pieces and an aloo (no egg, though the menu says you can ask for extra egg and aloo). The Chicken Rezala was a tad too sweet for my tastebud and again the Pasinda seemed to be ubderdone, quite chewy and hard. It looked obvious that the mutton dishes needed some more time to be perfected.

Overall the food was just okay and the most annoying thing was there were people standing beside your table waiting for you to leave. The management should look into this and either have a proper waiting place for them or at least not allow them to roam around the tables when people are actually having meals, makes one feel annoyed and irritated too.

##

2016-04-29 17:06:56
Sundeep N Bedabrata
42819
5.0
Shiraz in Kolkata is a legend for biryanis. A whole generation of Calcuttans (much before it was ‚ÄúKolkata‚Äù) grew up to its tastes. So much so, Calcuttans who have migrated often become nostalgic, to the extent of becoming emotional, over Shiraz biryani. The Calcuttan between us keeps looking for this style biryani in NCR. Insatiated, we recently visited Shiraz to see how did it fare with changing times.

Biryani is a cult. Aficionados do not mind travelling cities to have the perfect biryani. This complete dish mostly comprising rice ‚Äì meat ‚Äì rose water ‚Äì spices has evolved in various styles all over India.

Kolkata style Biryani is distinct from other varieties of biryanis. This style has emanated from the Awadhi style brought to Kolkata by Wajed Ali Shah during his exile. The biryani is subtly flavored with saffron, rose water and other fragrant spices. Plus it always comes with a huge boiled potato and is sometimes garnished with a boiled egg. It is far less spicy / strong in taste than the North or South Indian Biryanis.

Shiraz is synonymous to Biryani for any Calcuttan. It had humble beginnings God knows when. However, about twenty years ago, it used to be a spartan eatery at the prominent Park Street ‚Äì Mullick Bazar Crossing. People would not mind sharing tables with complete strangers, such was the leveling experience.

On a recent visit, we saw things have changed. This is now a fully air-conditioned restaurant with multi level seating and an annexe in an adjacent building. We ordered chicken biriyani, rezala, raita and firni.

Thankfully, the taste was intact over the years. The rice melted in the mouth while the flavours took over our senses. The mutton / chicken pieces were tender and could be easily separated with a fork (although fans would swear that fingers are the best option). The rezala was mild and helped in moistening the biryani.

The rice pudding - firni set in earthen pots was also mildly flavoured and sweetened. In fact, subtlety seemed to be their trademark, every dish was mild. This allowed diners to eat more without feeling uncomfortable.

We were told that Shiraz was not what it used to be. However, this experience belied all our apprehensions. Even if we are in Kolkata for half a day, we will surely try to have a meal at Shiraz.

2016-03-12 13:44:33
Fiery Chillies
33799311
3.5
One of the few places in Kolkata where I return once in a while for a fix of comfort food. The ambience has changed over the years, and have to say it looks much better than earlier. However, if you went there, you'd be wondering how weird it looked earlier :)

On my last visit, ordered for regular stuff. Mutton Rezala - nice creamy slow cooked mutton, swimming in fat. Problem with ordering this is, the staff will ask you why you are ordering this on its own and not with biryani .. it's my order ffs. Anyway, other stuff ordered were fried liver and mutton kebabs. The liver has been one of my favourites here over the years, and you can just have it melt in your mouth when you use a rumaali roti to wrap around it. Delicious. The kebabs are great too. Finished with a serving of their lovely firni, which isn't too sweet like many other places.

While the place is also known for its biryanis, I'd suggest against it - unless you are a fan of BIG servings of rice. For some reason, the rice is enough to feed 4 people and meat for 1 person. YMMV, and if you like biryanis, can check it out. Would also recommend a time other than evenings when it is less crowded. A late breakfast here on the weekends will be a good experience.

Verdict: for the service I'd gladly give 4/5. The biriyani is great and hence there is no reason not to visit the place again. But it won't be high in my list.

After a whole hearted recommendation by my friend I went here for lunch during my visit to kolkata. Known for its authentic biryani and non veg I really liked it but the hype was still not completely met.

It is a considerably big outlet in backyard of busy park street with good number of seating and basic dining environment. Decor is not much of a thing here as they mostly stress on food and service rather than a pleasing ambiance. Staff is good and always open to discussion regarding your taste preference for order. Service is real quick which shows how they have kept the ingredients mostly prepared.

As advised by them I ordered their Mutton Biryani and Mutton Stew with roti and ended my meal with phirni (kheer). Biryani was clearly authentic i.e plain with light flavors of rice with tender mutton and boiled potato. You can't expect much of a spice in a Kolkata biryani but the overall taste was still pleasing. Stew was average with ultra soft mutton but infused in a not so impressive gravy. Phirni again can be placed just near an average rating sweet dish. 

In all the place has got good side when it is judged on the basis of authenticity but still there is a lot of scope of healthy improvement considering preparations and flavors.

My Rating: 
1. Food: 3.5/5
2. Ambiance: 3.25/5
3. Service: 3.75/5
4. Value of Money: 3.25/5

##

2015-12-29 15:11:20
Somnath Chattopadhyay
29211665
4.5
It must have been 20 years, that I am visiting Shiraz at Mullick Bazar. It was at the other side of the road few year's back, with a non AC ground floor and AC first floor. Then it shifted to the other side of the road, and re-branded as Shiraz Golden. There are two outlets now with a gap of 50 meters between them.¬†

Shiraz and Biryani became synonymous to me during late 90's and early 2K. I can still remember the last time I visited there in 2002 before moving to Bengaluru with a new job. After 1.5 years, when I came back to my home town again, the first thing that struck me - I can again have Biryani from Shiraz,¬†

Coming straight to the food. Biryani to me, is mutton Biryani. With Chicken, you can have a good and similar dish, but the I cannot reach  the wholesome feeling with a Chicken dish. ¬†The quality of mutton and the cuts matter here. I accept, there are times, when I find the meat with a bit lower quality. But most of the time, Shiraz does full justice to their reputation. The rice is really long grain, and fluffy. The perfect balanced aroma is the winning factor for Shiraz, along with the perfect salt balance. Those, who cooks Biryani at home, can understand what I am talking about. It is very tough to reach that balance. Like a good whisky, you must taste this with Nose and Palate. The aroma should reveal a strong saffron note over a steady cinnamon base. Basically the base is created with a heavy dose of Garam Masala and Ghee. The meaty-fatty flavor gives a strong savory character to the aroma, which is balanced with a mild note of Kewda and rose water. Amazing balance. The texture has it's own character for Shiraz. Unlike the strong orange/saffron , it is much lighter is colour. The oil is nicely balanced, not dry, not too oily. ¬†Apart from Biryani, if you ask for two more dishes which are my favorite, are Mutton Pasinda and Firni. Just amazing. ¬† ¬†

Now coming to another part of Shiraz, which mostly unknown. It is their breakfast. Go to Shiraz around 6:30-7:00 in the morning, and try Daal-Gosht, Roti and Paya. It's another experience by itself. Before you come out after the breakfast, just don't miss the tea. Again you will be amazed.

##

2015-11-28 00:35:14
Aritra Chatterjee
29624833
5.0
I have been a regular at this place for the last 30 years. Not just me but also my entire family has been regularly visiting this restro and I have just continued the tradition. My parents often talk to me about the days when a plate of Chicken Chaap and rotis, sufficient for one person, would cost around Rs.5 (yes....you read it right...Rs.5).
Truly speaking Shiraz needs no introduction to foodies and frankly my review is just a tribute to the taste that they offer.
Originally this outlet was located on the opposite side of Park Street i.e. where presently GT Route is located. Today they have relocated to the opposite side with two centres side by side.The bigger one has a contemporary look while the smaller one has stuck to the traditional looks.Many of the old staff can still be seen today, serving customers . The cutlery is the same as of yesteryears.
In a nutshell the appearance of this age old restaurant has changed but the soul remains the same.

This place was the only outlet available back then. Increasing competition has seen many other outlets open in Kolkata but this one remains my favourite (Read: Nostalgia).
I consider the Mutton Pasinda and Mutton Chaap as their best items...with Mutton Biriyani a very very close second.Their Chicken items are also pretty good.
How can I forget their Mutton Rezala....oops I forgot the Shahi Stew....hey wait ...I just forgot to mention Iranian Chaap.
Actually the list goes on. You have to visit this place quite a number of times to savour their dishes.
For those with a sweet tooth:Do not forget to enjoy the Firni.
Restaurants may come and Restaurants may go.....but (for me) Shiraz will go on forever (Knock wood..üòá).
P.S. Try out a Chai pe Charcha with friends some evening.....the Tea is worth every buck you pay.

2015-09-27 01:39:30
Dev Sengupta

4.0
Shiraz. The reason Shiraz doesn't have a 4.0+ rating is because people go there with other Biryani in mind. Do. Not. Do. That.

Biryani: Since it is one of the legendary Biryani houses of the city, the Biryani is bound to be good. It is light and melts in your mouth. The golden brown rice here gives off an enticing smell, and you instantly notice it, which only increases your hunger. What a plate of Biryani begs for is a plate of gravy mutton. Screams for it, rather, and yes. They cook the mutton beautifully. The potatoes are cooked evenly and somewhat crisp to the fork or spoon. Beautiful. 

What saddened me though is the thin piece of meat I got. And I wasn't the only unfortunate there, all of my friends agreed that they didn't give generous portions of meat. Hence, the begging side tray of mutton. 

Would I go again? Maybe. Maybe not.

##

2015-09-15 21:06:17
Diptajeet Datta
199112
3.0
If you are from Calcutta, it is least possible that you haven't heard of this name - Shiraz. A brand on it's own terms, this restaurant is one name the Calcuttans swear by. The list is incomplete if you are talking about Calcutta-style biryani leaving out this name. I have been visiting this place since my school days since my school was nearby and it used to be my favourite restaurant at one point. So, during my recent trip to Kolkata I thought of revisiting some of those old tastes and memories. As decided, we were there on a weekday for dinner. It has been revamped and renovated a bit. The seats are more comfortable and the ambience is much better now with brighter lights. We targeted a corner table and took our seats. Instantly, a table attendant came to us for orders. We wanted to order chicken gilafi kebab and mutton seekh kebab but were informed that none were available. Infact most of the mutton kebabs and some of the chicken kebabs weren't available. Found it pretty surprising. Nevertheless, we settled for chicken bara kebab as starter, 1 chicken special biryani, 1 mutton biryani and 1 chicken chaap. The service was pretty good and prompt. The kebab was alright. The biggest disappointment was the biryani. The rice was dry and not at all moist. The chicken pieces were a bit hard and tasted like rubber. The mutton piece seemed like a joke  - a not a very meaty piece and was hard. The potato piece (probably the most desirable item in a Calcutta-style biryani) was well-cooked but tasted too bland and on the sweeter side. The chicken chaap was okay and tasted good. I was pretty surprised by the quality of food that was served to us  - definitely not the type I used to gorge on during my school days and absolutely not the type that was my favourite! The quality of food did not do justice at all to it's price. My impression of my once-favourite Shiraz has changed a lot after this visit. It is over-priced and over-hyped now. There are a lot of new restaurants in the city nowadays that are serving real good biryani, Shiraz will really need to pull up their socks to be able to compete with them. I am still very fond of this restaurant but sadly I can't recommend this to anyone now. True that it is a legendary restaurant but I really hope that it does justice to it's reputation/brand name. Good luck!

2015-09-06 09:06:12
Debdutta Ghosh
1067318
4.5
Occasion was my fairly good results in second year university examinations. Sadly didn't have enough time to go out and celebrate much, so it seemed to be a good idea to go with some quality biryani. Anyways I was craving for biryani for last few days, so to satisfy the craving, I thought of Shiraz. Shiraz is well known to everyone. It's one of those olden restaurants people talk about.

Located near Park Street crossing, the restaurant has shifted to opposite side of the pavement from last time visit. Sadly enough, they don't deliver to my area which is understandable. So I had to go there for a takeaway.

Food that I ordered was Chicken Biryani, Chicken Reshmi Kebab, Mutton Boti Kebab, Chicken Chaap, Chicken Bharta and some Raita to keep things cool. Chicken Biryani was almost perfect, very less oil used and no overpowering taste. Biryani is accompanied with a medium sized potato and a big piece of chicken. Chicken was soft and juicy. Reshmi Kebab was equally good, it was well charred and had a bit of malai on them. Boti Kebab were the best part... super-soft, just melts in the mouth. Chicken Bharta was good, a bit oily but still managable. Chicken Chaap was less oily compared to Bharta and tasted good. Raita was as it should be.

Pricing is on moderate scale, total cheque came around ‚Çπ1525 including taxes, which is normal these days. Quantity was good, don't get fooled by the biryani boxes as they may look small but packs huge quantity. Quantity of gravy items were also good. Kebabs were 6pcs per plate, very standard.

Service was fast, our order was served within 20-25 minutes. Surprisingly the place was empty so the order was served fast. Packing was good, no leaky containers. Biryani boxes were tied up properly for ease of carrying. Parking outside the restaurant is not a problem if you plan a takeaway.

Overall a much recommended restaurant to enjoy some classic Mughlai and North Indian food. If you haven't tried already, then you are missing out.

##

2015-08-16 22:11:31
Rajdeep Bhattacharjee
181052
4.0
We walked around 15 min to reach Shiraz Golden Restaurant, Mallick Bazar crossing, this place need no introduction to foodies. Probably the most famous place to get haleem in Kolkata, this century-old restaurant serves up many kinds of haleem. The chicken and mutton Haleem here are equally good, come here if you can't decide then try both or the mutton hydrabadi haleem if you're adventurous!

With haleems ranging from Irani and Afghani to Hyderabadi, you will have a difficult time deciding which to pick. I say go for the Irani Haleem, one of the most iconic haleem dishes in Shiraz's menu is their Irani Haleem. With no mistakes we ordered Irani Haleem and Tandoori roti. We were bit surprised to saw complementary coke with our meal.

Irani haleem here was just mind-blowing, the best till now, simply excellent. Although it looks rather simple, this medium bowl with a seriously runny haleem complemented with mouth-watering spicy flavours and a hint of lemon makes for a perfect way to start any day. Mutton pieces were boneless and they just vanished in your mouth.

After relishing all day delectable haleems (13/07/2015) we took a taxi from mallick bazar and within 5 minute reached Q33 (Quest Mall) to enjoy drinks & desserts for a good appetizing effect.

##

2015-07-04 12:12:30
Abhishek Das
64692
4.0
Shiraz needs no introduction to Biriyani loving people of Kolkata. Time to time Shiraz has proved itself to be the biriyani king of Kolkata, the awards hanging on the walls of the restaurant are the prove.
I have been going to shiraz since I was a kids, and if I remember correctly this is the place where I discovered the awesome taste of fragrance rice with succulent meat piece coupled with silky soft potato for the first time in my life.
I'm last couple of years everything has changed. The old shiraz now houses the upscale dawat e shiraz and right opposite to that houses the old famous, Shiraz the Golden Restaurant.
Decor wise this place looks modern with nice centralised air conditioning. Seating arrangements are quite comfortable. The ground floor is always full of people, while the upstairs the ambiance is quite and nice.
We knew we were late but still we asked for Halim and we got the obvious answer that it's not in stock. It was not disheartening but then we ordered 4 rumali roti, two tandoori roti, 1 mutton pasinda, 2 mutton biriyani and 1 firni for our sit and dine part. And packed 4 firni, 1 veg pulao, 1 paneer butter masala.
The rumali rotis were soft and made fresh and are huge in diameter. The tandoori rotis had the perfect softness and both looked and tasted perfect. Mutton pasinda was shredded boneless mutton in semi thick sauce. The pieces of mutton were well cooked melt in your mouth type and proved to be the perfect companion with the rotis. Next came the star of the show mutton biriyani. The rice was perfectly cooked and seasoned. The piece of meat was succulent and had its juices intact inside and the potato (which to me most of the people like in Kolkata biriyani) was perfectly cooked and had a mild flavours from the spices. The biriyani was light on the taste buds yet left the taste buds lingering and in desire for more. But as the stomach has its own limit we stopped. However not before we gulp down the mighty firni. The firni was chilled to perfection and was not overpowering sweet.
The service was prompt and the people were polite with smile on their faces.
Over all a great experience after a long time. Shiraz is a part of nostalgia and it's still satisfying people's taste buds.

It can be a bit difficult to find out, given to its location in park circus area but I would definitely be there again to try their biryani :)

##

2015-01-29 23:25:45
Abhishek Pal
2797818
3.5
The name of Shiraz is associated with all the Biryani lovers of the town.
I mean people like us have literally grown up with the Biryani bigshots like Shiraz.Back in the late 90s every second and fourth Sunday was meant for Mutton Rezalla,Tandoori Roti,Chicken Biryani and Firni.
No wonder I had put up so much of weight back then.

In the 21st century Shiraz stands out as the epitome of Biryani Restaurants in Kolkata.And this branch now being the oldest of the lot,has been made the headquarters of this famous chain of restaurants.
The price of a sumptuous platter of Biryani has gone up by four fold at least, but that antique smell still remains the same.
Having tasted the same dish from so many restaurants,and of course listening to the opinions of many food lovers,it is true that Shiraz Biryani makers add the Kashmiri Jaffran to the Biryani(maybe the only Biryani joint in Kolkata to do so).
And on top of that the egg also comes with the dish.

Due to stiff competition in the market the enthusiasm for Shiraz's Biryani has been hampered.As of now you get multiple food joints all over Kolkata serving the same dish,cooked in various styles.
One good thing about this restaurant is that they have introduced new dishes like the Murg Masallam which comes in half and full plate.
The kebabs of Shiraz bear a fresh taste and the tender juicy chicken leave a mark in your tongue....

My request to you foodies will be enjoy the taste of Shiraz,gulp down everything with a glass of Cola.I can guarantee you that 100% hygienic burp will be worth remembering!!!

This generation of food lovers like us really admire restaurant chains like Shiraz,which have maintained their standard for ages.What Kolkata needs now is a variation of the age old Awadhi Biryani which we are always having.
A new recipe will not only generate new business but also revolutionize the Awadhi Biryani.

2015-01-05 10:19:09
Sumitavo Paul
183369
4.0
Shiraaz is nostalgia for me. My uncle used to bring chicken chaap and tandoori roti during my childhood days (early 90s) and that was my first stint with mughlaai food. The tradition continued during my years at St.Xavier's College. Shiraaz was cheap and delicious - less impact on the pocket money along with finger licking food - a perfect combination for a college student.

The main dish at Shiraaz - Mutton Biryani is stupendous. A subtle taste with the use of fragrant spices - a lucknowi hint right here at Kolkata. The use of aloo is obviously the Kolkata culture going by the Bahadur Shah tradition.

Along with this Chicken and Mutton chaap - now you don't find the man cooking the chaap outside the restaurant all day long which used to be a regular affair earlier filling the air at Mullickbazaar with tremendous smell. The quality of chaap is still the same - it is not as spicy as the Royal Indian hotel version but definitely very good and unique in its own kind.

Other than this mutton bara kebab, chicken reshmi, kasturi kebab, fish tandoori are good but not exceptional.

In side dishes Mutton pasinda stands out - brilliant. Other than this Mutton Qalia, Korma, Rezala, Masala, Ghee kebab, Chicken kashmiri, Chicken masala are good - oily, spicy and tasty.

I would definitely recommend Shiraaz to all food lovers.

##

2014-08-11 11:24:48
Tom Roy
1171969
4.5
I grew up on "Shirazer biriyani" ‚Äì biriyani from Shiraz and their awesome, unforgetable chaap (mutton is my favorite, although the chicken is just as good), and every time I go back to the city, having the biriyani and chaap from Shiraz is a must. The biriyani is , of course, legend. There are many new places that have come up in that area, but Shiraz is top on my list. The biriyani is light, yes it is oily, but the taste is something that you get totally addicted to. The chaap is a greasy preparation of soft, on-the-bone mutton pieces that simmers on a large tawa for hours, and here again, this is what Kolkata memories are made of. Their rumaii rotis are fantastic as well and go really well with the chaap. The razela is world class, and the prices are totally reasonable. If, like us, you visit the city occasionally, Shiraz should be on your "must do" list.

Shiraz opened a branch in Dubai a couple of years ago, but it seems to have just disappeared. Which is a shame, really.

2014-07-30 23:20:23
Dr.Adwaita Nag
221626
4.0
Biryani for me has always meant shiraz... I did give a fair chance to the other restaurants,tasted all their biryani,but none could even come close....i keep coming back to shiraz...their biryani is out of the world..not too oily,non spicy,no overt smell of rose water,and the best part...the soft yummy potato-that cant be matched by any other shop... im sure they have some secret recipe ...the amount is more than enough for one person and you actually dont need anything to go along with it...still,greed always gets the better of me..for sides,i always side with my staple chicken chaap or rezala...both these two are oily but incredibly tasty...if you arenota biryani person,you can always opt for their lachha paratha-crispy and filling...
Food,i concede,is very heavy and filling...but you absolutely must keep some space aside for the dessert...Firni- it is the icing on the cake...a perfect ending.....and i assure you,once youve tasted it,you will never relish firni anywhere else...its top notch..
Shiraz is a very famed age old establishment...but it has stood the test of time...the current restaurant is a renovated version of the original resto that stood on the opposite side of the road..this one is more suited for family dining...the decor is minimalistic...go there only for the food... prices are reasonable...another great thing is they have an eye for hygiene..iv never had to return any of their dishes which is saying a lot (because at many of the other major biryani houses iv had a major hygiene issue...i would rather not go into the details)...
All in all..despite all the competition cropping up, shiraz is still the "golden" restaurant!!
Cheers!!

this review is a little late considering that I have visited shiraz quite a few times and have tasted a wide variety of their chicken / mutton dishes and their signature biriyani !!!   but then shiraz DOESNT REALLY NEED a review or introduction to any "Calcuttan".  shiraz now has about 5-6 restaurants all around Calcutta but this is the flagship outlet and I personally haven't tried any other of their outlets.

I personally call shiraz the top of the biriyani triangle in Calcutta (shiraz, arsalan and zeeshan constitute the triangle, btw).

Biriyani -- the shiraz brand of biriyani is light (not too oily and heavy i.e.) and yummy and belongs to the Awadhi / Lucknavi style - with the "Calcutta customization" of course - which is my personal favourite.  

of the chicken / mutton side dishes, the usual populars are always the "chaap" and "rezaala" because they are usually "safe" and can rarely go wrong!! chicken bharta is another favourite with most - it is shredded chicken in thick mughlai style gravy with half an egg.  I have tasted most of the side dishes here and these are the safest that cant go wrong with most.

of the kebabs, the haryali and tikka (spicy) kebabs win my vote.

writing this review, I am already raring to get back to Calcutta during the upcoming durga puja and dig into another round of biriyani and bharta!!

2014-02-03 01:35:20
Ronojoy Adhikari
1634283
4.5
Summary :  The place to go for an impeccable Awadhi biriyani. 

Details :  This place is a Calcutta institution. It has a no nonsense menu,  with a simple selection of kabaabs that pair well with the rotis, naans and kulchas,  mains of  quorma, chaap, rezala, pasinda, and kassa of both mutton and chicken, the flagship biriyani, with a firni or shahi tukra for dessert.  The  mains carry a stamp of authentic Lucknow origin : the quorma, rezala, pasinda and kassa are really what they ought to be, not the indistinguishable reddish brown gravies served in most "Mughlai" restaurants elsewhere. The biriyani remains one of its kind. Delicately flavoured and light, it is the perfect accompaniment to one of the mains. The service can be brusque, but the waiters do recognise regulars and manage to extend some courtesy through their overwork.  This is not a restaurant that scores on ambience or service but is one that is hard to beat when it comes to Awadh inspired cuisine. This reviewer, having frequented the restaurant for approximately thirty years, cannot agree with other reviews that claim a deterioration in quality.

It was the good old days of Shiraz and also for the people of Kolkata that whenever any discussion about quality biriyani was talked about Shiraz would always be preferred than the other players. And Shiraz would do justice in serving good Mughlai cuisine to the fellow people. But of late after having opened a large number of eateries all around the city their quality has tremendously fallen over the years. 
Thus I had wanted to pay a visit along with my few friends to this new place. The decor is decent and the overall ambiance is nothing great to talk about except some flashy lights spread over the dining area. We had ordered tandoori fish for starters and mutton biriyani and brain masala for the main course. To my utter disappointment I literally had no idea the quality can drop so drastically. The tandoori fish was total rubbish. It was not bhetki at all and the fish was stiff and dry. Fish kebabs are always soft which in this place it was. But it was not at all juicy and tasty might be because of the quality of the fish. Mutton biriyani is decent and nothing much great to talk about. Yes it was tasty but there are other players serving better biriyanis. The brain masala was good. It was soft and portion was also decent. The shahi tukra and the firni which was ordered as desserts were average. 
Again this place is serving good food but I am rating it as average because other restaurants are serving quality cuisine at affordable prices which are bench-marked. Thus in comparison with the other places the place is not at par.The prices are also not reasonable considering the quality they serve.Hope they might revive their quality in near future.

2013-08-17 23:45:09
Shubham Basu
924648
4.5
Shiraz has always been unanimous with biryani in Calcutta. Much before the days of Arsalan and other restaurants, Shiraz was the place to go for lip smacking biryani and chicken chaap. I have spent many evenings sitting in the rooftop garden, enjoying the sumptuous biryani, and watching the traffic go by. Though the rooftop garden does not remain anymore, Shiraz still occupies a place in my heart.
Shiraz has always been known for biryani, but I urge others, who have not been here and swear by the biryani of other restaurants, just pay this place a visit and you will not be disqappointed. The dishes that I would surely recommend are Mutton Biryani, Chicken Chaap, Mutton Rezala, Chicken do Pyaza, Chicken Bharta and Chicken Kassa. Each of these dishes come cooked in a pool of lard, but when the food tastes so good, who bothers with the calories? A meal can surely never be complete without their firni, which is like a porridge, made with milk, rice and mawa. It is flavoured with rose water which gives a very pleasant after-taste. Shiraz is surely recommended for each and every biryani lover in Calcutta.
PS- Tea is present on the menu, however, one cannot order only tea. Some food dishes have to be ordered and the tea can accompany the order.

Before beginning, I have to say, I am slightly biased towards Shiraz. That said, giving this place ratings which is just about okay might sound harsh. However, it is necessary.

For a brand which constantly is promoting itself as the "Authentic Kolkata Biryani", that is unacceptable in my book. I checked my companion's piece of meat as well, and his turned out to be dry too. And decidedly chewy.

The pasinda was great though. Slightly bony, but great. It was what I would curl up with along with a couple of tandoori rotis.

I thought... okay, this is just one incident, and maybe the next time I go it would be changed.

Next time I went there, I was in a group of four. We ordered a biryani, two chaaps, a pasinda, two burra kababs and one chicken tandoori along with naan. Chaap was okay, but nothing to write home about. In fact, my friend thought it was too salty. 

Service was fast, but also very abrupt. Our water glasses were banged down in front of us. It is not acceptable when the prices are not average.

3.0
YUMMRAJ Demystifies the Legend of Shiraz

In a nutshell:

A long History of excellence, sadly struggling to keep up with its earlier Glory - A lunch here left us with a cold feeling & also food that was surely lower than expectations.

Short Description - In case u r in a hurry:

Shiraz as a name rings a bell with Most Calcuttans (since the Days when Kolkata was Calcutta). I have had many good experiences in the past here like many others. Over the years I have seen a decline & had stopped going here & insead to the newly opened Arsalan. Similar experiences cud b heard from others as well. This time around I made it a point to revisit Shiraz & check it out myself................ 

There are two restaurants at Park Street Mullickbazar area. One is a few shops away from the other. The newer one is closer to the crossing & the older one is a few shops away. The newer one is swankier as well. We decided to go to the Old one.

The old restaurant has a non airconditioned ground floor & an airconditioned first floor. Furniture, look & ambience of the first floor is much upgraded as compared to the ground floor. The look at first floor was that of an old Eightees restaurant. Cubicles made with set of sofas facing each other. Lighting was dim.

The staff of this place need a special mention. Some of them seem to walk out of a 70's movie. They have been in the same job of waiting tables for decades, have got bored enough & that shows on their face every moment, appear at the tables like robots without any facial expression & at times frown if too many questions are asked. The uniform has quite a 'Nawabi Khansama' look. The relatively younger Manager who I guess was the only person in suit, was also quite serious faced. He was continuing to speak to me in English even though I was speaking in Bengali. It was then that I did what I do best - mentally poke. I striked a conversation on 'what is popular here / what is legendary here, I have come from far to eat here/ what is 'mash-hoor' (famous) here etc & within 3 -4 sentences each, the customer - server barrier fell apart. We were talking to each other as two human beings & the interaction was excellent since then for the rest of our stay.

The food is surely very good in isolation but as compared to others, this one takes a beating - Straight away from Arsalan Park Circus & surely from Aafreen, Metiabruz. We were unlucky to get stale meat in one of the dishes, very happy to get a replacement after we reported the same & even more disappointed when the replacement turned out to b stale as well.
 
Detailed Description - In case u have the time to njoy reading:

We started our Lunch with a starter recommended by our server - Mutton Burrah Kabab. He said 'This is the best among all starters on offer'. We were served 2 pieces of the Burrah kabab, one of which turned out to be stale meat (first bite was horrifying). The other one was absolutely fine. It seems they were from two different goats.  We complained about the meat & we were offered a replacement of both the kababs. We said 'just replacing the bad one is good enough'. We were told that since Burrah takes 20 minutes to make, it wud take 20 minutes & it wud b good if we ate the biryani before the burrah. So did we.

The burrah was perfectly spiced, excellent to taste but had a serious problem with texture. The pieces of the burrah that were hanging loose / the pieces towards the outside of the burrah was perfect. However the meat adjacent to the bone (1.5 cm from the bone) was raw & red (like in steaks that are rare). I personally did not dislike it coz to me it was like a steak with Indian spices but I am sure most people will not b able to appreciate it. Taste wise this get 4.5/5 & texture wise it gets 2.5/5. Overall the good Burrah gets 3.5/5. 

The replacement burrah was much better than the stale one but was just about 70% fresh. That was surprising & I have a problem with it - Once is an accident but second time is callousness (I heard the server tell the kitchen that this was a replacement). Stale one gets 0/5 & that takes the plate of Burrah to 1.75/5.

Shiraz serves Kolkata Biryani - for the uninitiated, Kolkata Biryani is an offshoot of Lucknowi Dum Biryani that was introduced to the population of Kolkattans when Nawab of Lucknow Wazid Ali Shah was deported from Lucknow to Kolkata by the British. The nawab brought with him his huge entourage of chefs & nauch girls. The chefs left a lasting impression on Bengali cuisine - Kolkata Biryani, Chhamp, rezala, korma etc are an integral part of Bengali cuisine now. 

Like the Lucknowi Biryani, the Kolkata Biryani is also slow cooked under low fire by sealing the container (Dum cooking) & the meat & rice is cooked together so that the flavors of the meat & the rice intermingle. The Biryani is characterized by flavorful long independent grains of rice that are super-soft melt in the mouth & meats that r super soft & least fibrous (due to long period of cooking). A whole potato & a boiled egg is also customarily served. There is hardly any salan served anywhere with Kolkata Biryani.

We ordered the Shiraz Special Mutton Biryani. The rice was long but not extra long. The grains of rice were independent but not super-soft 'melt in the mouth'. The flavors & taste was however very good. I wud give this 3.5/5.

The meats were not at all super soft. They were not as hard as well. They were just about ok - If I were served this food at some outlet in Gurgaon, I wud have maybe accepted it. However, sitting at Shiraz in Kolkata, this was far below expectations. Good in terms of taste & flavors again. I wud say the meat gets 3.5/5.

Overall the Biryani thus gets 3.5/5

We ordered two side dishes with the Biryani. One was a Chaap that has been famous for decades. Chaap is mutton rib marinated in masalas & tawa cooked over a long time. The pieces were not presented like usual mutton chops but as abruptly chopped mutton rib pieces. That made the eating part quite weird - difficult to make out which is the meat & which is the bone. Taste wise it was very good & so were the flavors. I wud give this 3.75/5.

We also went for Mutton stew. This is not at all linked to the European Mutton stew - infact they wud faint on seeing this stew. This is a mutton curry with loads of ghee, spices & an oniony base. The taste of the gravy is awesome & so r the flavors. Some Mutton pieces were very soft & nice. Others were pretty fibrous. I wud do a 4.5/5 for the gravy & a 3/5 for the meats. That makes the overall 3.75/5.

We ended the meal with Phirni - the photo of the phirni on menu card showed strands of saffron. The phirni served to us had not even one strand. The taste was very flat & quite boring. To finish it was becoming a challenge. I wud give this 2/5.

Thus taking into consideration all individual dishes, the overall score comes to 3/5. 

The newer Shiraz Golden restaurants in the other parts of the world seem to be doing good but the old original one is in a state of neglect. I hope someone from the Management reads this & does the needful.
